<Author>BucksCounty4Me
<Content>Friendly Staff, Updated decor, Good location! Our family of 4 just returned from a long weekend at this Embassy Suites in Wash. DC. It was our first visit to this hotel and we were very pleased. I had selected it based on past tripadvisor reviews and we were not disappointed at all. This hotel is a very friendly and active place -- all the staff we came in contact with had super attitudes and were very helpful. They take pride in their work and it shows. We had a regular room -- all are Suites - which include one bedroom and a sitting room. The whole place was very clean and had fresh, updated decor -- including fashionable bedcoverings, curtains and furniture. There was a large flatscreen television in the living room portion of the suite plus a sofa (which could convert to sofabed), chair and a small kitchen table with 4 chairs. There was also a small sink in the living room and a small refrigerator, microwave, coffee maker, iron/ironing board, and private small safe for valuables. The bedroom contained 2 Queen beds which were very comfortable and had particularly soft sheets, blankets and bedspreads. All the linens looked brand new. The bathroom was large with a long counter, hair dryer, lots of towels of various sizes and a tub and shower combo with massage shower head. It was also clean and in good condition. The hotel has a small gym which my husband went to several times and said was adequate for his needs. It was often busy but there was never a time when the gym looked overcrowded or anyone was waiting for a machine. The gym equipment was also updated and in good working condition, along with flat screen TVs to keep you occupied while you were exercising. There was a small indoor pool off of the gym area but when we were there is was chock full of young children doing cannonballs and splashing -- a little too loud and rowdy for our tastes. But, I guess this is sue to the fact that we visited at a time that kids are out of school due to the Winter Break. I don't think that the pool experience would be one I would recommend to any adult who doesn't have young children. If you do have young kids, though -- this is a good place to let them burn off some steam. (Better in the pool area than the Atrium at the breakfast buffet!.....more on that later!)The breakfast buffet was a highlight of the hotel. I had read previous reviews and took their advice into account when I chose the first time our family visited the buffet. The first time we came early as suggested and it was a very pleasant experience. At 7:15 am it was not crowded and it was very calm and relaxing. They have large screen televisions with CNN morning shows on throughout the atrium and also provide complimentary newspapers. The Embassy Suites DC breakfast buffet was really very varied and included many hot and cold items...certainly something for everyone. It was one of the best hotel buffets that I have seen -- and our family travels frequently.There was an Omelette Station which consisted of a very friendly chef asking you which fillings you would like (spinach, bacon, tomato, sausage, onion, cheese, pepper, etc...) and he prepares it fresh right in front of you. Very tasty. There is also a Make Your Own Waffle station which had 4 or 5 machines where you could pour your own batter into a waffle machine and in 2 minutes you'd have a crispy waffle to eat. There was also a standard buffet set up of chafing dishes that included scrambled eggs, pancakes, sausage links, bacon, homefried potatoes and oatmeal. There was a large tray of assorted Yoplait yogurts and a large bowl of diced melon, plus individual fruits like whole bananas and oranges. They also had a selection of muffins, bread and bagels (and toasters for them). There was a large selection of breakfast cereals, mostly kid-friendly stuff like fruit loops, Frosted flakes, etc. -- all popular name brands. Big selection in the beverage department --- Coffees were from Starbucks and included several different flavors (decaf  regular) as well as hot chocolate. They also had various choices of milk and hot teas. They had self serve soda fountains which included all the major flavors (coke, diet coke, sprite, etc), plus juice machines which included orange, apple, fruit punch and cranberry. The only problem we encountered with the breakfast buffet had to do with the timing of our 2nd visit (which I had been warned about from past tripadvisor reviews!). If you visit the buffet anytime after, say 8:30 on, you are in for a different experience. The place is VERY crowded then and there are often not enough seats for everyone, plus, at least during our visit, there was a large volume of unattended young children. This is not really any fault of the hotel, of course, -- but the fault of inattentive parents who probably just assume that their children are safe within an enclosed area so they let them run free....(hence, the problem). Our children are 8 and 10, so they are past the constant running stage -- that age from about 3 - 5 when toddlers, (especially boys!) are in perpetual motion. The problem with this situation was that there was such a high density of people in a small area. Adults were trying to carry heavy trays of hot food and steaming coffee through crowded, tight spaces and little ones, oblivious to the dangers overhead, were running in and out and weaving around their legs, Of course, this behavior is just part of what being a kid is all about, but this is just not the place for it due to the safety issues. Watching a well dressed businessman who is not in the mindset of having to be wary of a 3 foot high obstacle coming at his knees at high speed was something to see! You could just see that there were a whole mix of ages in one place and that the older people without children were dumbfounded that some very young children were left unsupervised (with the possibility of getting hurt due to an accident) or that young elementary age children were going up to the hot waffle makers alone to cook their own food. One specific incident that stands out in my mind was when our family was trying to get down into the breakfast area and we were walking down the ramps that lead into the space. We came across a young boy (maybe 4 years old) dressed in red footed pajamas laying on his side and rolling himself the length of the ramp (kind of like a human swiffer, if you will) People had to carefully tip toe around him so as not to step on him! At different times throughout our 20 minutes at breakfast I looked back over to where the boy was rolling and, sure enough, he was still there...spinning away like a bowling ball through a crowd of human pins. STRIKE! One of the biggest compliments in my review has has to go to the hotel staff at the breakfast buffet -- They were all very pleasant and, since they were all very busy, they should be commended for being so upbeat in the midst of all this activity. I even saw an award hanging up in the cooking area of the Omelette Station noting an excellent achievement the breakfast team received recently. It is certainly well deserved. Any time I interacted with them they were all smiles -- I also saw them cleaning up many a spill or a splatter with happy faces and positive comments to other guests. I was impressed with their excellent attitudes - and somewhat in awe that they could deal with this barely organized chaos day after day! So, all in all -- an excellent stay at this very busy, active, and updated hotel in the center of DC action. You won't be disappointed here....just remember to get up and eat your breakfast early! HAPPY TRAVELS!

<Content>Great stay, would highly recommend Just returned from a lovely one night stay at the Embassy Suites.Took the train from our home in VA to attend an evening performance at the Kennedy Center. Easy metro trip from Union Station-then about a four block walk from the Dupont Circle stop through a nice neighborhood of upscale townhomes and apartments.. Two room suite spotless and spacious with wet bar, small fridge, microwave, coffee maker with tea and coffee selections. Enjoyed complimentary cocktails at manager's reception prior to delicious dinner in Nicola's- their on site Italian restaurant. When we told them we had limited time for dinner as we needed to get to the Kennedy Center, they could not have been more accommodating, suggesting entrees that took less time to prepare. We were out in plenty of time, and bellman got us a cab when we were ready -$6.50 each way.  We enjoyed a quiet and comfortable night's sleep. Individual temperature controls for each suite worked well.Extensive breakfast buffet with an omlet station the next morning was a bit crowded with families, but this was a holiday weekend, and we chose probably the busiest time to eat-around 9 am. But tables were cleared promptly and we had no difficulty finding a place to sit-there is lots of room. We stored our luggage at the hotel while we visited some museums prior to our early evening departure on the train-we will definitely stay here again on our next visit to DC.

<Content>Exceeded expectations The host hotel for my conference couldn't accommodate us for the duration of our stay so we were happy to find this hotel close by. Not only do the suites make life easier (separate bedrooom so if one of us wants to go to bed early or get up early, there's additional space to hang out), there's an extra sink outside of the bathroom, there's two TVs and lots of outlets for electronics. Best parts though were the included hot breakfast buffet (made to order omelettes, waffles, etc), but the manager's evening reception which was any well drink, draft beer or specialty drink they could concoct -- especially friendly staff, snacks that were different each night (veggies and rip, chips, pretzels, nachos w/jalapenos and cheese) and the opportunity to feed the koi (if so inclined). OK, yes, it's a chain and had that kind of Holiday Inn feel with the big atrium and waterfalls and generic room furniture, but the rooms were clean, fairly modern, quiet and again, the staff were especially friendly and unobtrusive. For the money and great location (close to Dupont Circle), I wouldn't trade it for something more typical DC.

<Author>RandT3
<Content>Convenient and Classy Property While in town for a convention, I spent an evening at this property in one of the Conference Suites. The room was enormous and consisted of a large conference room with a 12-seat table, a wet bar, oversized bathroom and large bedroom. The suite was a corner room, so I was able to enjoy the view as well. The front desk was very accomodating, and allowed me to check in far earlier than normal. Check in was quick and efficient.The concierge was able to arrange last minute transportation for me to Alexandria, VA. I was disappointed that the shuttle could not take me, but the independent van driver was excellent, albeit expensive.Room service was wonderful and quick. AM breakfast was better than I had expected, but very, very busy. There are both hot and cold self service offerings and a great selection of beverages.The only problem I ran into was the wireless internet service. I use a Mac, and never have any connection issues when using public wi-fi. Normally, a lack of internet service doesn't pose a problem, but I had a presentation to edit and needed dedicated service. The front desk was again attentive and walked me through the steps necessary to connect, but it was of no help. I gave up and tried again much later that evening knowing that the hours between 6PM and 9PM are very busy for hotel connectivity. BY 11PM, I was connected to the Hilton E-Help desk in Texas and a technician walked me through everything. I was able to connect from that point forward. Sadly, I was charged the full rate for the service and would have been very responsive to a discount or service comp for the time and trouble...oh well...I got a great deal on the room, so no loss. There are a number of nice restaurants within a two or three block radius. I chose to take the Metro into Maryland to meet friends, and was amazed at the ease and convenience of the public transportation system.Overall, this hotel did an amazing job. The staff was friendly and attentive, and to me, that was the most important aspect of my stay.

<Content>Where Do I Begin I can't even begin to tell you all how wonderful this hotel is. It is a beautiful hotel that has an open atrium with waterfalls and fish in the ponds. The foliage is lush and the sounds from the water are tranquil. The hotel offers a complimentary breakfast and complimentary drinks and snack (at 5:30 pm). <Author>TNTnVA
<Content>Loved it! We will definitely stay at this embassy suites when we go back to D.C. The atrium is beautiful. The room was very nice, although in my opinion the living/dining area was a little plain. The flat screen tv was nice. The bedroom was very nicely decorated and very quiet. Breakfast was great (scrambled eggs, bacon, sausage, grits, oatmeal, waffles, omelets, fruit, yogurt bagels...) and we never had a problem finding a seat. The manager's reception was also a great way to unwind in the evenings. Our 3 year old loved having snack and soda, and also loved the kids movie that plays on the 2nd floor mezzanine each evening during the reception. She also enjoyed getting to feed the fish a few times. We walked to 3 different metro stations from the hotel, and didn't consider any of them too far, in fact we actually enjoyed walking through the city. The staff is excellent!!! One thing, the pool was much smaller than we expected, so we didn't end up swimming as planned. Also, they have a computer in the lobby right by the front desk that you can look up local attractions/restaurants etc - don't use it, ask the staff instead. We looked up drugstore, and it pulled up a CVS that was like 8 blocks away, only to find on the walk home that there is a walgreens 1/2 block away. Anyway, I highly recommend this hotel, particularly to families.

<Author>Toronto215
<Content>Happy with my hotel choice in DC I just spent 5 nights at the Embassy Suites in Washington DC. We checked out the reviews of many hotels and chose this one because of the size of the room. We are a family of 5 (kids are 14, 12, and 9) and it seems that most hotels only have room for 4 people squished into 2 double beds. My wife and I slept in a king bed in a bedroom and the 3 kids slept in the main room. Two shared the queen pullout and we brought an air mattress for the other. 2 TV's, one bathroom, overall perfectly fine for us and better than spending $$ on 2 rooms. The managers reception is daily from 5:30 to 7:30 and we didn't miss a day. Cold beer, veggies, nachos, chips, popcorn etc. The kids made use of the small but adequate indoor pool almost every day. We had friends who stayed at the Westin Grand around the corner and they spent their spare time at our hotel which was much more fun for the kids.The decor is not the greatest, but the hotel was clean, comfortable, and the service was very good - including the restaurant. The location seemed fine. I would certainly go back without hesitation. Not a cheap hotel by any means, but nothing is in Washington...

<Author>Dave1485
<Content>A Decent Hotel After reading many of the reviews on Trip Advisor I was a bit apprehensive about this (and other) hotels on our recent vacation to the East Coast. Our four night stay at the Embassy Suites was quite pleasant. The food was OK, and much better than what we had at many places on this trip. The morning breakfast had some lines but what would I expect from a hotel with nine or ten floors. We made it a point to get down there early enough and our breakfasts were always hot. If I had to define a criticism of anything on this stay I guess it would be that the front desk personnel didn't seem very friendly to me, but they were usually pretty busy with waiting on customers so that's understandable too. We would definately stay at the Embassy Suites again. Our son loved the pool and game room, the elevators were fast and the location was very convenient with a pharmacy/convenience store on the corner and a Starbucks next to that. The traffic in Washington was absolutely horrendous, but that wasn't the hotels fault, :), and in spite of that we still managed to take the van out and about the city on numerous occasions because we had very convenient underground parking with our room.

<Author>lynnlynnTravel
<Content>Good hotel and location My husband, 14-yr-old son and I stayed here for 6 nights at the end of July. We took a cab to/from the hotel (~$17 ea way). It is within walking distance of the metro, but if you have luggage I would recommend a cab instead (you never know when the escalators may not be operating plus it's just a hassle to try to drag luggage around on a metro). We had a suite (dining room, living room w/ flat screen and pull out queen bed, and separate bedroom w/ king bed and tv), so there was plenty of space and the refrigerator and microwave were useful for leftovers. The room was clean and spacious, and housekeeping did a good job every day.The breakfasts are pretty good -- you can make your own waffles, or stand in line for made-to-order eggs, and they have everything else buffet-style - scrambled eggs, pancakes, sausage, biscuits and gravy, hash browns, cold cereal, juice, coffee, muffins/danishes, yogurt, etc. You do need to get there early enough so they don't run out of something you might want (such as fruit). They are also very busy unless you get there early.We did not go to any of the manager's cocktail parties, or use the pool or fitness rooms as we ended up either returning late in the evening, or, on the few days we got back early, we were too tired from the walking and heat to do anything but relax in our suite.We also had 1 dinner at the hotel's Italian restaurant. We found it to be pretty good, better quality than we had expected for a hotel restaurant. Price-wise, it was about what you would expect from a hotel restaurant. (For fun restaurant, we really enjoyed the Capitol Grille on Pennsylvania Ave....it was expensive, but it was a really neat atmosphere. )I would recommend this hotel for a family or business trip. (The reason I rated it 4 stars rather than 5 is I thought their rates were a bit expensive)

<Author>TravelerMR
<Content>Close to everything Stayed for six days in early August. The staff was friendly and provided good suggestions on getting around and directions. We walked to Georgetown University and Lincoln Memorial on two different days - on other days we used the metro to travel. The manager's reception had good drinks and plenty of soft drinks available with different munchies each night. The breakfast was good, but very hectic in the last hour of serving. Perhaps making it a bit more family-oriented would result in more people eating there in the evening. However, there were plenty of more family-oriented restaurants in the area.

<Content>Good location, but you might do better We spent 4 nights at the hotel. The room was very nice and a good size, with 2 TVs and a fridge which we found very useful. The things we found a bit disappointing were that the concierge never seemed to be about when you needed assistance, and the advice given at reception proved inaccurate on several occasions which almost made us make some very poor decisions in our planning. There never seemed to be a good time to get there, and finding a table could be tricky. It was always very busy. And my final concern was, I am sure, not a regular occurrance, but we arrived back at the hotel mid-afternoon to find our door and the door of the room next to ours open, with no cleaning or maintenance staff anywhere near. Indeed no-one came to the room in the 1/2 hour I waited. I never did get an explanation as to why they had left our room open for anyone to walk in.

<Author>jcjohns91107
<Content>Great vacation My family and I stayed at the Embassy Suites DC over 4th of July weekend and had a great time. I used Hilton points to book the stay, requesting the two bedroom presidential suite, and actually got it. The room was huge! Two full bedrooms and two baths, living room, dining room. Way more than we needed but the kids loved it. Flat panel TV's in each bedroom and the living room. The service was very good. The staff always helpful. There was a water leak over the bar area that was fixed in a flash. I guess the only complaint would be the air conditioner was quite noisy so I guess if you were a light sleeper you might have problems.As with all Embassy's, full breakfast is included. Being the 4th of July weekend, it was pretty crowded each morning but the food was fine and we were always able to find a table. It saves a lot to be able to eat a free big breakfast each day.The location of the hotel is great. It's a quiet area close to DuPont Circle. There are many restaurants within a 10 minute walk. The Foggy Bottom metro station is a 10 minute walk away which will get you anywhere. We walked into Georgetown one day with no complaints from the kids.I would definitely stay here again.

<Author>joan3boys
<Content>Number 1 in DC? No Way! We have been here for 4 nights and are leaving tomorrow. We have stayed here many times before and thought the value was excellent, but now we feel differently. We paid $ 399 for our room and it is not worth it. the room and hotel are starting to show their age. The hallway carpets are old, buckling and filthy, the wallpaper in the room is peeling off and stained, the room carpet is in terrible shape and the trim needs a good coat of paint. the pool is the size of a matchbook and is way too small for a busy hotel this size. there are about 10 chairs for 400 guests. After sightseeing all day, this is not a relaxing pool to be in. The tiles are moldy and falling off and the ceiling tiles are off because of leaking.My husband was the only one to do breakfast this morning and he stood in line 3 different times, each one for 15 mins. He then sat at the only available table that was dirty with dishes and syrup. He said next time he will go somewhere and pay for breakfast.The only great experience we had with this place were with the bartenders at the manager,s reception - they were excellent. The location is good, about 5 long blocks each way to the 2 metro stations about 15 mins, but there are many hotels in this area.I guess we are just getting old and less tolerant with crowds and busy hotels. We figured next time for the money we can stay somewhere nicer and have a relaxing time instead of being annoyed.

<Content>Are there two Embassy suites? I chose the Embassy Suites based on its #1 popularity, and previous fine experience with the chain in three other cities. Around 11 PM the front desk offered us a choice of some portable fans, and to move us to a smaller room. We chose the latter and fortunately was very comfortable. Except that there was only a King Bed and a Fold Out Sofa, so the kid was back to banging his shins on the metal bed frame. When I left I inquired if there would be any adjustment in the $489 rate as we had a smaller room without the two beds, and was told it wouldn't be possible as the hotel was so busy.Location: A $10 cab ride (plus tip) away from everything and anything. Or, a l-o-n-g hot walk to tour bus stops, and public transit. Summary: your customary Embassy Suites with a good morning breakfast, and evening happy hour. Just a strange location.

<Content>Would definitely go back to this hotel We stayed at the Embassy Suites which I chose based on Trip Advisor reviews. We were very pleased with our stay and would definitely recommend it. The staff was very friendly and very helpful. The rooms were clean and spacious, more than enough room for my husband and I and our 12 and 14 year old sons. The extra sink in the bedroom came in very handy when getting ready. The location is good, about a 15 min. walk to the White House and about 10 min. to the Metro if you don't feel like walking to the sights. The hot breakfast was good and convenient (you don't have to worry about finding a restaurant or paying ridiculous prices for cereal and coffee). My son enjoyed making his own belgian waffles each morning. Yes it can be busy in the morning but we just went down 1/2 hr earlier which was no big deal. If you like Italian, there's a great little restaurant close by, Luigi's. Overall, we had a really good experience with this hotel and would return.

<Author>RMarkT
<Content>Great Experience at the Embassy Suites - Washington D.C. We recently returned from an eight day vacation in Washington D.C. and stayed at this Embassy Suites Property. Our family of five, including two teenage girls and a 12 year old boy, booked two spacious rooms that met all of our needs. The property is located in the NW quadrant of the city and is a short walk to all of the sites including the White House, the memorials, all of the Smithsonian museums and Georgetown. We walked everywhere and when we didn't want to walk we took the very efficient Metro which was only three short blocks away. The hotel rooms were clean and comfortable. The small refrigerator came in mighty handy to store lots of water and snacks that were bought at the Walgreens or CVS which was only one block away. (along with the Starbucks which for me was a necessity). The free breakfast in the morning combined with the free cocktail hour at night put the icing on the cake for us. This hotel made our stay in Washington D.C. much more relaxing and enjoyable. I highly recommend the Embassy Suites in Washington D.C. at M and 22nd streets. One hint for families traveling to D.C. in the summer. It's hot so stay at this hotel and walk three blocks to the large free public pool for a quick refreshing dip.

<Author>joybob
<Content>Great value! We arrived in around 5:00 and received a warm welcome from the staff. Our room was spacious and comfortable and it was great that everyone had their own bed. The loveseat in the sitting area folded out into a bed. My daughter who slept out there did complain about the noise so be aware that that noisy neighbors can be heard from this room. The evening reception was delightful and very much appreciated. Beer and wine and various drinks were served as well as soda and juice. There were munchies that my family of four enjoyed. During the weekend the place was milling with kids. We have two teenagers so this did not bother us at all. The complete breakfast was the highlight and it does pay to get up early to avoid a long line. The one morning we slept in there was still plenty of food. There are coin laundry machines for those who desire to do some wash. There is a walk of a few blocks to the metro which under normal circustances would never have phased us but because there is so much walking/standing in DC we did feel quite tired by the end of the day. We ordered a delivered pizza from Luigis (just okay). We ate dinner at Johnny Rockets, (decent and 50's atmoshpere) a Chinese restarant right around the corner that was decent, TGIF (great food but just okay service) and The Front Page in Dupont Circle which was excellent in every way. The hotel was a great bargain in every way and I would highly recommend it to families wanting to visit DC. If you have young children, you may want to tour with a company that picks you up and drops you off due to all the walking you will end up doing if you tour on your own.

<Author>motherofsix_8
<Content>Perfect Place for a Family to stay in D.C. We (my husband and I and our six children ages 14 to 3) stayed for two nights in two connecting king suites. The staff was very plesant to us. They even arranged for us to park our full size van at the Marriot Hotel accross the street, because our vehicle was too tall for their underground parking garage. We had plenty of room to spread out! Lots of soft chairs and the bedding was so comfortable. The corner suite had a dining table with six seats, while the other suite had a table for four. The manager's reception was a little different both nights. We only drank the soft drinks (serve yourself machines), but they also served cocktails. The first night they set out fresh veggies and dip with potato chips and pretzles. The second night there was salsa, guacamole, tortilla chips and pretzles. Both nights they also had popcorn. The kids enjoyed filling up their tray with some before heading back to the room for watching TV. In the morning, the breakfast was wonderful. In addition to the made to order omlets, there was also, scrambled eggs, bacon one morning and sausages the other, pancakes, oatmeal, potatoes, and make your own waffles. You could have cereal, yogurt, muffins, toast, bagles, and fresh fruit, too. There were different kinds of coffees, tea, milk, and juices. We never had a problem finding two tables of four for all of us to sit down to eat. We filled up here so, we only needed a light lunch and plenty of water while sight seeing! We were pleased that the hotel was in walking distance of all the attractions. We did not use the metro. We walked from 22nd Street to 15th street, then took Pennsylvania Avenue to the White House. We started out just before 9 a.m. and managed to see all the memorials in the morning and the Air and Space Museum along with the Museum of Natural History in the afternoon. There was just enough time for a swim at the hotel's pool (which was not that small and there is also a hot tub) before the manager's reception. We enjoyed ordering pizza from Manny and Olga's who delivered to our room. It was delicious and just $20 for two pizzas! We retired to our room that night to rest our tired feet. The kids did not have to fight over the TV since we had four! We left the next morning after breakfast. The Iwa Jima Memorial and Arlington were our last stop before heading home to Indiana. Anyone who asks us about our trip to Washington D.C. will also hear about the two wonderful nights we spent at the Embassy Suites Hotel. My kids will tell you it was the best hotel they ever stayed in!  
<Date>Jul 7, 2008

<Author>nydoc
<Content>good- a bit overpriced hotel itself is very nice. Positives-good location, breakfast included, nightly open bar reception with cheap snacks, big rooms with flat panel tv, frig, microwave, kid friendly. Negatives-- not cheap (free breakfast, recption etc is not really free- its part of your room rate which was 350+ a night during late april ), managers recption is really fair wine , watered down frozen drinks etc. with pretzels, chips--not real food in the evening although kids were happy), slow elevators with other kids often pushing all the buttons, a tiny indoor pool that is as overcrowded as ive ever seen and completely overrun with kids (and i love kids!!), extra charge per day for in room internet-insane!, small computer terminals free in lobby often were nonfunctional, parking was in the hotel 1 block away --same charge as lot in hotel always too crowded, one day the maids just never came--several phone calls lead to this being rectified at 730 pm after being out the whole day. All in all would stay here only if i had kids and while i would return it would only be with a better deal on the room. Will likely consider other places although all in all it was nice --keep in mind the above and look for a discounted rate.

I noted some reviews about the number of children in the hotel, and some other negative comments, but also noted the high rating on tripadvisor and booked it for 5 nights.We arrived and asked for a room away from the elevator and were given one, but as it turned out there were NO rooms at the elevator in the design of this hotel. While one could still hear the ding of the elevator when it came to a floor, you could NOT hear ANYTHING from the rear bedroom. And we NEVER heard our neighbors in the hotel...either from side to side, or from above. The rooms were spacious and the flatscreen TV with high-def channels was GREAT for the limited time we were actually in the room.The breakfast buffet was the best we have ever had at an Embassy Suites hotel! The potatoes were actually seasoned with appropriate spices and there were excellent options for omelets, waffles, pancakes, fresh fruit, english muffins, pastries, and nice strong coffee!While there were MANY children in the hotel, we never saw that as a problem during our stay! There were also internet kiosks in the lobby to allow you to print off boarding passes or check email.After we settled into the room, it was dinner time and we asked at the desk for a restaurant recommendation, and were told it was a short walk to Georgetown, which was full of restaurant (and we later learned, shopping) choices. It was THEN that we learned that this hotel was such a great choice for central location in Washington, DC!So enough for the hotel, absolutely no complaints! To travel around DC, check out the Circulator bus! It travels from Union Station on the west of DC through Georgetown on the east side, from the river district on the east on a north/south loop to the convention center, and on a weekend loop around the mall, all for $1 per trip, or $3 for an all-day pass! Much cheaper than taxies, saves on walking (and there is a lot of walking in DC), and the buses run very frequently.

<Author>adventuremam
<Content>Great Place For Families Great hotel for tourist travel to DC, particularly with kids. Very family friendly. We were there for a week this June and found it to be a perfect location to see all the sights. We took cabs to the museums from the hotel and never paid more than $13 for the trip (with two per day, that comes to the same price as parking a car at the hotel). The included breakfast every morning is tasty and extensive and my son loved the managers reception every evening for snacks. I also can't say enough positive things about the staff. They were friendly and helpful with directions, flagging down cabs, and keeping the rooms and the grounds clean. The biggest downside to our stay is that we appeared to be there during school field trip season, so there were large swarms of somewhat unsupervised kids using the public areas. While this is a downside, it is certainly not the fault of the hotel. The Itallian restaurant in the hotel was very good, and there are a number of other restaurant options in easy walking distance of the hotel, through nice neighborhoods, including a number of embassies. Tip for tired sightseers - there are several local restaurants that will deliver to your room! We stretched a tasty Thai dinner out for two days. SInce the rooms are equiped with microwave and refridgerator, eating in the room is a reasonable option as well.

<Author>IUScott
<Content>Reliably Good We've stayed at this Embassy Suites several times over the past 10+ years (both before and since our son was born), which I suppose says enough. While the property doesn't wow, it's dependable, comfortable, and pleasant.The location is great--out of the immediate bustle for downtown but part of the vibrant Dupont Circle area. The Mall, Georgetown, and other attractions and neighborhoods are a very manageable walk away, but the Metro station is nearby if you want to catch a train.The breakfast buffet is a nice perk. It's diverse and substantial enough to satisfy a full range of appetites, from those wanting a healthy, post-workout refresher to those who view all-you-can-eat as a challenge. The evening reception is OK--worth going to if you're sitting around the hotel but not worth hurrying back for. The snacks are standard reception fare, with the healthier options being particularly uninspired. Likewise for the beer and wine selections. The frozen drinks--popular with many--are crazy sweet. Still, there are various soft drinks and juices available too.If you're craving a good workout, there are endless great places to run from the hotel. If you want to stay in house, the workout room is well-equipped for being as small as it is. Likewise for the pool/whirlpool/sauna area. It can be a raucous kid-magnet at times, but there are also a couple adults-only hours each day.I've taken to describing this as our default hotel. Until something else comes along with a better combination of location, price, and amenities, we'll keep coming back.

<Author>rhondala79
<Content>Great trip,great hotel We recently stayed here for 3 nights over the memorial day weekend. This was our first time in Washington DC. We traveled with our 2 sons ages 18 and 10, and another 18 year old friend of our sons. We really were impressed with this hotel. Check in was very smooth and pleasant. The room was very clean and well appointed. Even though there were 5 of us, we had plenty of room. We liked the 2 TV's and the big flat screen in the living area was nice. My 10 year old missed having the Disney channel on the cable, but we weren't there to watch TV anyway.  With 2 teenagers along, we were up late and slept late, so we never went down to breakfast before at least 10:00. Breakfast was awesome, and even with the hotel being full, and the lateness of the hour, there was always plenty of food. Of course you can't beat the price-FREE!! We had been on a cruise in March, and my youngest said it reminded him of a cruise breakfast. Thus the free brunch carried us through to late afternoon. The location was great. We were just a few blocks from the Foggy Bottom/GWU metro station, and we found out just how convenient that is. Metro is the only way to travel to the sites in DC. Also great was the area-it was very clean, and appeared safe. You were within a few blocks of all the charm, restaurants and shops of Georgetown and Dupont Circle. The fact that a Walgreens, Starbucks, and a great Chinese restaurant were right across the street were tremendous bonuses for us as well. Our 10 year old had a great time at the pool every night after doing so much walking to see all the sites. Yes it is a small pool, and did get a bit crowded, but that didn't bother Marc at all. The 18 year olds were pleased to be able to surf the internet for free at the computer kiosks. The concierge and front desk were very helpful as far as helping us get around to where we wanted to go, and things to do. We will definitely stay at this hotel again when we are in DC-which could be within the next year. There just is too much we didn't get to see in such a short time.

<Author>SomecallmeTim
<Content>Perfect for families with kids We stayed at Embassy Suites DC last week and were traveling with a 2 year-old and 5 month-old. This place was perfect for our needs and had extra little perks that made it the best experience of our trip. Great location a pleasant walk from the Dupont Circle Metro station. <Author>Skittykitty
<Content>Great location and great price We booked this hotel almost solely on the recommendations from this site and were really glad that we did. The location is great (about 25 minutes walk to the White House) and the price is too. The rooms were clean and very spacious, the staff were helpful and polite. Having the living area on the inside of the atrium meant that we weren disturbed by the noise of the waterfalls, but if that space was used for sleeping it could be a little noisy. The all-inclusive breakfast was varied and plentiful. It was fine for food to be taken back to rooms. We went down around 8am each day, but noticed that even at 9.30am there still seemed to be plenty of everything. The Manager Reception was a great plus. The quality of drinks and snacks wasn amazing, but then it is free and we could go back for a second round. The on-site restaurant was fine, but not very exciting. The shop is handy and open until late. The hotel is very family friendly, which might put some people off but we weren there to sit around in the hotel so weren bothered by the number of children. The pool was pretty small and occupied by lots of children, which was a shame but to be expected. There is a charge for internet access in rooms, but there is a small business centre (3 PCs) and also two PC near the elevators, which was fine for the occasional checking of email. We had a really great stay here and would thoroughly recommend it to others.

Because of the location, there are plenty of other dining choices not too far away (loved Marakesh Palace!) Dad and kids enjoyed the indoor pool and hot tub (especially after a full day of sightseeing!) The staff was also very helpful, and there is a free Internet kiosk in the lobby so you can plan out your day. We will definitely return to this hotel!

<Author>CStoneTX
<Content>Spring Break at Embassy Suites My husband, two children (ages 6 and 8), mother-in-law (MIL) and I stayed at the Embassy Suites for 5 nights over spring break. We had a room with two queen sized beds, and MIL slept on the pullout sofa in the suite. Overall, the room was a bit crowded for the five of us, but since we were sightseeing all day, it worked just fine. It's the perfect size for a family of four. We were on the 5th floor, overlooking N Street, but were never bothered with outside noise. The breakfast and snacks in the evening were great. Even though the hotel was fully booked, we always were able to find a table. The line for home made omelets was long on a couple of the mornings, but only when we ate a little later. They also gave out fish food at 9am and 6pm, so the kids could feed the goldfish in the ponds in the atrium - that was fun for our kids.The pool was my kid's favorite part - even though it was small, they enjoyed swimming in it. The water hurt their eyes, but once we got them goggles it was fine. The older kids rough-housed quite a bit in the evening, so I would recommend using the pool earlier in the evening or in the morning if you have younger children. There's also a fairly nice fitness center. There were 4 or 5 treadmills, each with its own TV. Also an elliptical and a recumbent bike. And some free weights. The treadmills were always available early in the morning or in the evening, but I did walk by around 9am one morning and they were all in use.Regarding location, it was a bit of a walk to the two nearest metro stops. Foggy Bottom was about 3-4 blocks away - while that doesn't sound like much, when it's cold outside and the kids are tired, it seemed like a lot further. Dupont Circle was a bit closer. There were plenty of good restaurants within walking distance. Also a Starbucks just a block away, as well as a Walgreens to stock the fridge in the suite with snacks and drinks. The only thing that irritated me was that there was a fee for the wireless internet access in the suites. However, they had several computer stations set up in the lobby with free internet access, and printing available in the business center. I was always able to find a station when I needed one, even though the hotel was full.Overall, we were very pleased with the hotel. Even though the cost was a bit high, everything was included in the room charge except for wireless internet access. I didn't feel like I was being nickeled and dimed like at other places. This is a great place for a family to stay while in D.C.

<Author>RLCTapmom
<Content>Nice hotel, kids loved it My husband, two daughters (ages 6 and 8) and I stayed at the Embassy Suites for 3 nights. We were impressed by the size of the room considering the location of the hotel (being so close to downtown Washington DC). The room and bath were clean and modern, and the room had a microwave and small fridge. The kids bed was the sofa in the living room, and it was nice to have our own bedroom. The pool was sort of small, but it was clean with tons of towels and the kids loved it. Also, they were able to go into the hot tub so they wanted to swim each day as much as they could. There also was a game room which had about 6-8 machines for the kids. Breakfast was plentiful and although the hotel was full, we had no problems getting a table each morning and having plenty to eat. Between 5:30 and 7:30 in the evening, they had an open bar with snacks (popcorn, chips, salsa, etc) which was great for us to chill out after a day of sightseeing. The staff was friendly and came right to our room when we needed anything. As for location, the hotel is in a nice area and there is a Starbucks within a block, which we loved. The Metro was a few blocks away and cabs were plentiful when we preferred to take them. Overall, a great stay - we will return when we get back to DC!

<Author>nikkitouchton
<Content>Great stay, perfect hotel for families! We stayed here for 3 nights (Fri.-Mon.) in mid-March on a tourist visit of D.C. Although we did not actually bring our child with us, this is a great hotel for families. All rooms are suites with separate bedroom(s) and include a small fridge and microwave. Very clean hotel with great staff and service. We enjoyed a very nice dinner one night at the hotel restaurant Nicola's (Italian/American cuisine). The morning complimentary breaskfast (if you upgrade to the stay for breakfast and not just the standard complimentary breakfast available to all guests)includes a buffet with all the traditional breakfast foods, including made-to-order omlettes, though as busy as the hotel is and with all the families and children staying here, breakfast time is hectic and is better if you get there very early, like before 7:30AM. There are afternoon complimentary snacks, beverages, and alcoholic drinks (for adults of course) for all guests. For the price (if you book a good deal early), this hotel is a great value. George Washington Univ. Hospital and a Fire Station are just a couple blocks away so be ready for their alarms to wake you in the night if your room is streetside (we were on the 6th floor and heard them very well, though we easily fell back asleep after a long day of touring). The Metro is 4 blocks away. DuPont Circle is very close too with many good restaurants. I would definitely stay here again. This was my first Embassy Suites expereince and I will definitely look for them in other cities when I travel.

<Content>Nice hotel - but did not meet expectations We just returned from 5 nights at this hotel, which included president's weekend. We picked the hotel because it was rated #1 on this site. <Author>Jakuch
<Content>Very Nice Property We stayed at the Embassy Suites near Georgetown from Dec. 25-20, 2007. I must disclose upfront we are Hilton Honors Gold members and received an upgraded room. And what a room. It had a dining room and living room and bedroom, two flat screen tvs and was well-appointed. It was probably the nicest upgrade we've received so far as Gold Members, although the Disneyworld Hilton was pretty great, too. We had two teeanage daughters and one slept on the pullout sofa and the other, for some unknown reason, slept on two lounge chair pushed together with extra bedding. At least they weren't kicking each other all night. The nightly refreshment hour varied, but the drink offerings were always good. They had two kinds of slushies that alcohol can be added to, if you want. They also had all kinds of sodas and a full bar with decent brands of beer  wine. The snacks ranged from veggies, dip, chips, and pretzels to (one night) just chips and canned salsa. The breakfast was a standard (i.e. good) Embassy Suites offering with pancakes, bacon, eggs, and all kinds of pastries and cereals. The juices were the watery, dispensed kind and not good. Management greeted folks at breakfast.The restaurant was Italian and the food (the pastas tasted fresh made) was good but service was inexperienced. Turnover must be problem here. The pool and hot tub area was clean and warm -- nice during winter. Plenty of towels restocked.The location was a bit of a walk if you weren't cabbing it. We generally took a cab out in the morning to see the sights and took the Metro back home in the evening. We mostly exited at Dupont Circle and walked (downhill!) to our hotel. The area is residential and felt very safe for our family.Overall, I would very much stay here again. The property is on the high end of the Embassy Suites experience.

<Author>Boston-traveller40
<Content>Excellent hotel, excellent location My family (2 children aged 7 and 11) have just returned from a long weekend at the Embassy Suites, Washington DC. Overall this is an excellent hotel; very well designed, atrium style complete with waterfall, fish pond, and glass walled elevators. Rooms are spacious and clean with lots of granite, plasma TV, refridgerator, microwave, coffee maker. Included is a complimentary hot breakfast which was pretty good, and also an evening managers reception (i.e. free snacks and drinks/cocktails) between 5.30pm and 7.30pm. The hotel is a few blocks from a Metro station, so very convenient for exploring DC. We did not need a car at all during our stay. It is also close to a number of good restaurants. We tried the Front Page restaurant, and Luigis, both pretty good. Our only complaint was the pool, which was quite small, and therefore always felt crowded. The hot tub was also small and with 3 people in it felt like being in a bathtub. Children were allowed in the hot tub, so it was rarely empty. Apart from that, this really is a very good hotel and I would definitely stay here again on my next visit.

<Author>PinballSeeker
<Content>One day in DC We stayed at the DC ES on Friday Feb 8th for a single night. We are a family of 4 with 2 children (9,7) so a safe well located place with 2 rooms and an easy breakfast is very important. This hotel fits that bill nicely. Absolutely no road noise (except for the rare siren), comfortable beds, and a breakfast that allows even the most picky eaters to find something (e.g. pancakes, eggs, sausage, fruit, cereal, made to order omalettes, waffles, coffee, juices, and on and on) made this an easy choice. Admittedly, we tend to prefer to stay at ES's, so the fact that this one was rated #1 in the city made this a no brainer. I do like the fact that ES tend to be very consistent, and this one was no exception. Parking was about $24 a night for indoor self parking, Internet was about $10 for the day, but I got the impression from reading all the other reviews that these charges were similar to other area lodging. The view from our 8th floor (of 9 in the building) was basically another tall building but this hotel is surrounded by simliarly sized buildings, so if a view is essential to your experience, you may need to inquire at the desk or go elsewhere. U shaped pool with 3 and 4 foot sections were perfect for our sprites. Small gameroom is there, and I saw the exercise area but did not get a chance to look at it. I believe there was a new Starbucks about 2 blocks away along with a CVS pharmacy. Metro is about 4 blocks. All in all, it was a good experience and with only one day to spend, so I took no chances. About $145 with AAA. Hard to beat.

<Author>mccarthys5
<Content>It's a solid 3.5 star hotel...and a great deal We stayed at the Embassy Suites for one night - 1/5/08. It is a very good hotel. Hotel is located in DC's West End, with close proximity to Georgetown and Dupont Circle.Since we were parking for a weekend night (Saturday), we pulled around to park in the hotel parking garage and the valet pointed out there were a couple of spots for free available right on the street in front of the hotel - SO nice of him! We parked for free for the night right in front of the hotel and saved the $24 per car. The parking spaces are apparently good until 7 am Monday morning. Great start to our day/night in DC!Check-in was quick and they accomodated our group of 9 with 2 rooms directly next to each other on the 9th floor. Rooms are all suite-style with a living room - sofa bed, dining room table, plasma TV, fridge, microwave, coffeemaker, sink in the living room, coffee table - all were in very good condition. Bathroom is normal size for a hotel room and was clean, but not luxurious. Sink, toilet, shower/tub combo - however, the shower had low water pressure.Our bedroom had 2 queen beds with a sink in the bedroom as well (that is 3 sinks overall in the suite!) and another TV in the bedroom (not plasma, though.) Bed is reasonably comfortable. We had a nice view of the National Cathedral from our suite. Utilized the indoor pool and hot tub - fine, a little outdated, but suits small children just fine. Hot tub was nice and hot. There is also a sauna and a fitness room as well - entrance is via the 2nd floor.Breakfast is typical of all Embassy Suites - served buffet-style, complimentary and lots of choices. Made-to-order omlettes are a good bet - you choose the fillings. There are many choices, both hot and cold - eggs, pancakes, sausage, bacon, muffins, bagels, cereals, pasteries, juices, coffee, grits, fresh fruit, yogurt, granola, etc...etc...you just can't go wrong with the ES breakfast. We also went to the complimentary manager's reception and they had 4 different beers on tap (Heineken included!) as well as preminum liquors (like Bacardi.) You can have as many drinks as you like from 5:30-7:30. Snacks are definitely munchies - chips and salsa, popcorn, pretzels, that kind of thing. They also had a movie playing right on top of the manager's reception for the kids - our evening they were showing Cars - great idea to keep the kids engaged. Every evening they change the choice of movie shown.We ordered room service for dinner from the hotel restaurant and this is the only thing I did not like about the hotel. The food was awful. I had shrimp alfredo and it was overcooked shrimp with barely any alfredo sauce, overcooked pasta and the entire dish was cold by the time I got it. Just awful. 3 of the 4 adults in our party ordered it and all of us felt the same way. The bruschetta I got as an appetizer was decent, however. Nonetheless, if I return to this property, I will avoid the hotel restaurant - really a bad meal. Our kids meals (we ordered 5 of them) were all cold and overcooked as well.Embassy Suites is always a great bang for the buck. I paid $135 for the night per room directly through the hotel website and for the free drinks, the free breakfast, the large suite-style rooms, the indoor pool and the overall kid-friendly atmosphere in a central DC setting, I probably couldn't do any better in terms of value for the dollar. I'd return without issue.  
<Date>Jan 9, 2008

<Author>morrinme
<Content>Excellent! Our singing group of 8 women traveled to Washington at the beginning of December. (We were singing at the White House.) We booked 3 rooms at the Embassy Suites.Upon arriving, we were greeted warmly at the desk, and were treated wonderfully by EVERY employee the entire duration of our stay. Everyone is friendly and helpful - we were just so blown away.In the middle of the first night, the hotel alarm went off and everyone had to head to the lobby. Again, the staff answered all questions and put people at ease. (False alarm.) The following morning the night manager circulated at breakfast, explaining why the alarm had gone off and asking everyone how they fared the night before.Speaking of breakfast - WoW! There is so much to choose from that I can't imagine anyone would go away hungry: hot and cold cereals, pancakes, waffles, bacon, eggs, made-to-order omelets, biscuits and gravy, fresh fruit, and much more... all included in the room rate.The rooms themselves were very clean and nicely decorated. The bedding is crisp, clean and comfortable. A few of us slept on the sofabeds and they are comfortable and clean, as well.Again, we were thrilled with the hotel and plan to stay there again if we return to Washington. ***One word of advice about the taxis...get a quote BEFORE you get in! The prices are supposed to be standardized, but we were charged widely different amounts for our day trips.

<Author>Cancun_curious
<Content>Good hotel, esp. for those with kids My husband and I stayed at the Embassy Suites Washington, DC for two nights for a getaway. The price was quite good. The hotel is in a wonderful location, in DuPont Circle but in a quiet area, within a 10-minute walk to the Georgetown Area. The gym was excellent for a hotel gym. The pool was nice, but the jacuzzi was broken. The hotel offers adult swim late, which is probably very nice. When we went to the pool, there were kids having fun, which was fun to watch but not good for relaxation. The breakfast was very good, however the cleaning staff will clear your place when you get up to get more food. The staff was all very nice. One problem: the room heat turns off automatically when you leave the room to conserve energy. This is very good for the enviornment, however, when we returne to our room, it was FREEZING. It took quite a while to warm up. The hotel is great for families with kids, b/c of the extra bed in the sofa in the suites and the refrigerator/microwave in the room. The kids there all seemed to be having fun. On the other hand, if you dislike children, you may want to consider another hotel.Overall, it was a good hotel and I would recommend it.

<Author>Kimba57
<Content>Perfect weekend getaway From the friendly staff to the luck of being placed in one of the larger suites, this was the perfect place for a girls' weekend getaway. My 2 friends and I felt extremely at ease in the neighborhood and walked everywhere! We did not dine on site, so I can't really say anything about the Italian restaurant except that it looked like a nice place and the menu prices seemed reasonable. The buffet was typical for ES, so no surprises there. The pool/jacuzzi area was also typical for ES, but not crowded with kids (possibly because of the time of year). It's a pleasant walk to Foggy Bottom metro station just a few blocks away if needed. Also, the hotel is about 4 or 5 blocks from Georgetown, so we visited there a couple of times for shopping and brunch at Martin's Tavern. No complaints at all about our suite, which was very large, very clean and had comfortable beds. Great exercise facility on site!My only gripe is that the jacuzzi/pool maintenance is performed at a time of morning when I wanted to use those facilities. It would be nice if it could be done during the hours when that area is closed to guests.This was my first time visiting DC, and I look forward to the day I can return. I would definitely stay at this hotel again.

<Author>Sadie_NB
<Content>Good for families First and foremost, this hotel is great for families. And that is why it's packed with families. If you really don't like children and want a peaceful breakfast, I recommend staying elsewhere.The breakfast was great, particularly for a family. The buffet was wonderful and the coffee nice and strong the way we like it. The food was actually decent, if they remember to bring it to you. We went twice and regretted it twice. Other families had the same problems on different days so it wasn't just an isolated experience.The pool was fun for the kids and they also show movies in the afternoon for kids. Given the outreach to families, I wonder why they don't have a separate play area for younger kids. Not even late checkout when I tried. Kevin or Keith (sorry, I can't remember his name correctly) is a wonderful bellman who is friendly to the kids and adults alike.

<Author>Tucsontourist
<Content>Loved the Beds! We were guests, and were treated to a non-smoking suite. The room was very nice, with a wide screen plasma tv, a couch, desk, microwave and fridge ... all very nice.The bedroom was very nice and the bed was delighhhhhtful.. it had a down-like comforter and lots and lots of pillows. I wish I had realized that sooner in our stay.There's a manager's cocktail hour from 5:30-7:00 every night (never attended) and a nice breakfast buffet that isn't as wonderful as other places, but it's certainly fine to get the day started--I'm guessing kids would like it, too.The business center is down in the basement which was a bit inconvenient, but there is an Internet kiosk in the hotel lobby to sign on and check your email or surf the web.All in all, very nice.

<Author>TravelingJournal
<Content>Can't beat the price and location For less than what you would pay for in other hotels in the area, you get to have a suite for you and your family. That's why we booked this place, because it is all suites and they provide you with evening reception (of snacks and drinks) and breakfast which is all complimentary to our booking. Just breakfast itself saved the 4 of us at least $30-40 a day, and after 4 days of doing this, the savings does add up. Something of note though for the drinks. The other embassy suites I have visited did not have limitations as what kind of drinks I am allowed/not allowed to order, but the lady who was making drinks during my stay told me that something as simple as long island ice tea could not be made for free due to management policy, whatever the heck that means. All the other Embassy Suites provides me with the drink I want!The rooms are exactly as expected from an Embassy Suites. A small mini-bar/sink is in the livingroom area, which helped in the 4 of us getting ready in the morning a bit quicker. The sofa does convert to a sofabed which helped in providing more room to sleep in.One thing I noticed at our stay though is, because I am a Hilton HHonors member, we were given the 9th floor (top floor) of this building which was designated as a HHonor floor. I don't know if this how it's arranged at all other Embassy Suites, but the floor was less crowded with people, the views better, and it just felt good to be on that floor. Good job.You do pay for your parking at this place, but you really don't need a car from here. Subway stations are all walking distance, and if you do want to come back to your hotel from any place in DC, just take the cab. Parking within DC for travelers is a mess, and it's not worth the headache. Just use mass transit.My only gripe with this hotel was also the breakfast. I found moldy white bread in the bread dispensers, which I notified the staff members. They quickly took away my bread, but did not check through all the other white bread within the dispenser to make sure they weren't moldy. I did a quick take on the bread, and they seemed to be ok, but it would have been more reassuring if the bread was checked again by staffers.I would stay here again. Besides the moldy bread incident and the alcohol limitations, I had a great time. We paid $159 + tax per night btw.

<Author>tcaruanj
<Content>Great Hotel! Good Location! I stayed at the Embassy Suites in Washington DC from October 10th until October 12th 2007. This is the Embassy Suites around M and 22nd Street - not to be confused with Embassy Suites Convention Center. I did not stay there.I would stay at this hotel again. It was great. We had a very large room with a queen bed. 2 tvs, one in the bedroom and one in the lounge area. A large eating table which would double as a work desk. A good sized bathroom and 3 sinks! one in the bathroom, a bar sink in the lounge and another sink in the bed room. There was a bar fridge, coffee maker and I think a microwave as well. The room was very clean and the service was excellent. you can self park on the property as well which we did and it has in and out privilages. there is free internet access in the hotel - so even if you don't bring your notebook with you there are kiosks in the reception area you can use. There is a decent gym too.I was pleased with the room and with the service. they called us when we got to the room to ask us if everything was ok. Our fridge started to leak so I called down and they came up immediately, changed the sink and dried the carpet for us.you get a free breakfast which you have lots to choose from. I'm a picky breakfast eater so I wasn't nuts about what they had but I still found something. they have fruit, yougurt, hard boiled eggs, cooked to order omlets (I found them kind of greesy and the mushrooms are canned so I didn't care for it), make your own waffles, pancakes, cereal, juice, bacon, scrambled eggs, etc. Location wise, this place is great. you're close to Dupont circle metro and close to Foggy Bottom. you're walking distance from George Town were all the stores are. you're walking distance from the white house too. Actually we walked to all monuments - some were a bit of a far walk but it's doable (could be up to a 45 min to 1 hr walk). But if you don't want to walk to some of those further sites, pop on the metro and you're there in minutes.In terms of food, I read one comment that there wasn't much around there. Actually there is lots of food around there, you need to stay on M street there is lots of food there.

<Author>ArizonaTraveler77
<Content>Perfect family hotel with a great location Based on reviews we read in Trip Advisor for families travelling with children, we chose the Embassy Suites hotel on 22nd Street (Foggy Bottom area) in Washington DC. We could not have been happier with our choice! We were travelling with our 3 children ages 16, 13, and 6 who had never been to Washington before. The hotel was in a fantastic neighborhood location, a short and easy walk to the subway and with plenty of neighborhood restaurants nearby. We like to use local transportation when we travel, so this was a real plus. Since the room had a seperate living area (with a sofa sleeper), it gave the 5 of us plenty of room to spread out. The room was nicely decorated and very clean. One of the best features, especially from a family perspective is the free breakfast...not a continental breakfast, but a full buffet with lots of choices. They managed to feed a huge number of people, but kept everything stocked and clean. The staff at the hotel was excellent as well, very service oriented and willing to answer all our questions, in fact, one of the bellman took us under his wing and explained the whole subway system to us in detail, which was a big help! We will definitley stay here again and would recommend the hotel to anyone travelling to Washington DC.

<Content>The Perfect Place! I go to this wonderful hotel every year for my annual girls' road trip with some girlfriends and co-workers - and we have never failed to be delighted! Also, we got a call from the hotel restaurant (where we ordered a very nice pizza from) asking if we liked the food. <Author>puppymama1
<Content>Highly recommend this Embassy Suites! We stayed here for 4 nights (9/29-10/2/07) while visiting Washington DC. We both loved the hotel which is within a 10 minute walk to either the Dupont Circle (Red line) or the Foggy Bottom (Blue or Orange line) metro stations. The room was lovely - we had a corner suite and it had 2 flat screen TVs, one of which was HD, a dining table, wet bar, microwave, refrigerator, coffeemaker, good sized bathroom and king bed. The free breakfast was great - made to order omelets, plus a large buffet selection of grits, potatoes, eggs, bacon, sausage, bagels, rolls, cereals, oatmeal, fruit, danish, a large variety of juices, soft drinks, coffee, tea, etc.. We ate a large breakfast each day then skipped lunch which saved us a lot of money! Every evening the manager's reception had FREE drinks - beer, wines, margaritas, strawberry daquiris, and various other liquers, along with pretzels, popcorn, potato chips and snack mix. It was a nice way to unwind from the long days we spent sightseeing. The hotel was in a very nice and safe area and we never felt nervous about walking to or from the hotel. The Chinese restaurant Meiwah is only 2 blocks away and it was one of the best meals we had in DC. I'd skip the restaurant in the hotel -- it wasn't all that good and it was fairly expensive. There is also a CVS store a few blocks away - hard to find so ask someone where it is if you want to get some water, soda, snacks, etc... All in all we had a lovely stay and would highly recommend this hotel to anyone visiting Washington for business or pleasure!

<Author>BKlein
<Content>Great family hotel - not for business We had a very good stay here and would recommend this hotel to anyone travelling with kids. Just a couple issues worth noting. The business center was overrun with children playing computer games all the time. That made it impossible to use a computer when needed. I need to stay in touch with work even on vacation (as most people do I expect.) I access my email on my blackberry, but cannot print and find it difficult to read long messages which show up as attachments. There are standup computer stations throughout the lobby, but those did not solve my printer problem. I guess the long and short is that I think business centers should be for business, and the family slant of this hotel means there are no 18 and over rules for the business center. It was a relatively minor inconvience for me, but if I had been travelling on business it would have been a huge problem. In a similar vein, we had a lot of delays caused by tween kids having races in the elevators. One last thing - I called the concierge the second night of our four night stay for dinner reservation assistance and had to leave a voice mail ... I am still waiting for a call back. All in all, for a family trip at well under $300 a night it was just fine. Delightful personnel (the woman who cleans up during breakfast is one of the nicest service workers I have encountered in a long time!) <Author>EDSALLKIDS
<Content>DC GETAWAY Stayed here for 3 days in August with a family of five. The hotel is in a nice safe area of Washington DC, just north of the George Washington University campus. There were 2 other hotels on the same block, a Marriott and Ritz Carlton. The suite was a standard room for Embassy Suites hotels, with a good size living room area that had the pull out sofa bed and 2 double beds in the bedroom. The room was very clean, but had a bit of old and new in it. The living room had a flat screen TV with HD, while the bedroom had a standard one. Sinks had granite tops, but the tub/shower and toilet were dated and a bit beat up. The decorating was a late 80's, early 90's vibe, but overall for the price, compared to other DC properties it was well worth it. The breakfast buffet had a nice spread, but I agree with other reviewers that it was crowded and not easy to find a seat. I saw many people taking their trays up to their rooms. The restaurant in the hotel Nicolas was a solid choice if you don't feel like going back out for dinner after a day of sightseeing.Please note that the hotel is quite a ways from the major attractions. Walking to them is possible, but we mixed in cabs with the walking. There are 2 Metro stations nearby, but we figured with a 12, 9, and 4 year old with a stroller, cabs would be easier than lugging everybody to a train.Overall a pleasant stay and a solid hotel. The atrium interior was also fun for the kids, as they got a kick out of the fish. It probably shouldn't be rated #2 overall in DC, but definetely #1 for families looking to visit Washington.

<Author>Gastropod
<Content>Very good but crowded On the strength of Tripadvisor recommendations, we stayed at the Embassy Suites at the end of July.It was generally very good but just a little tooooo popular! They provide complimentary breakfast as well as a complimentary happy hour. At breakfast, we initially found it difficult to get a table for our group. To the hotel's credit, they spotted this problem for us and for many others and extended the breakfast serving times by an hour. Breakfasts were then okay although still crowded.Our suite was very good indeed although somewhat formulaic. I was disappointed at their daily $9.95 charge for internet access but particularly enjoyed playing with the high definition tv in the room. It was very useful to have a fridge and microwave in the room as well.Like breakfast, happy hour was served in the large atrium which forms the centre of the hotel. This was very pleasant but lacked the tranquility one might hope for. This was partly due to the many excited small kids and teenagers running around (well, it IS a family hotel) and also to the 2 storey tall water feature. This had waterfalls which made a lot of noise. That coupled with the general hubbubb made for a fairly noisy environment. We were glad of the air conditioning in this area though!There is also a pool and fitness centre. We did not use these facilities, having tramped around the Washington sights all day. There are two coin operated laundries in the hotel but these were also very popular. It was difficult to get a time slot. The hotel also offers a document printing service. I did not use it so I do not know if there is a charge for this.The front desk was generally very good and it was possible to check out automatically without having to queue up to settle our bill. That was well organised.For location, the Embasy Suites is not too bad. It is situated in an inner suburb of Washington but not immediately near any centres. The two nearest metro stops are Dupont Circle and Foggy Bottom. Both are around ten minutes away in foot. The historic and very picturesque area of Georgetown is also an easy stroll and there are very many good restaurants there. It is possible to walk to the White House and nearby attractions in around half an hour to 45 minutes. Washington's public transport system is good, cheap, clean and modern and gives good access to these areas.All in all, we would agree with the good ratings. It was a busy, well run hotel but we were uncomfortable with just how crowded it was. That said, it was well managed and operated and they coped with the hordes of people very well.

We stayed in an executive suite (I think that's what they called it). It had a bedroom with two queen size beds and then a living room/kitchenette room with a nice TV and a sofa bed. The breakfast buffet was nice but I recommend you get up early to eat because it gets really busy after 8am. The manager's reception is kind of lame. Popcorn, chips and salsa. Not too much fun if you're not a drinker. We didn't really spend time in the pool. We live in Florida so pools aren't a big deal for us. We ate at the hotel restaurant one night and it was okay; nothing spectacular but everything tasted fairly good. We were in DC for the 4th and that was great fun! We stayed away from the Mall and watched the fireworks sitting in front of the Federal Reserve building. It was the perfect spot, no crowds! The hotel staff was very friendly and met our every need. The cleaning staff was great, too. We came home to nice, clean rooms every night. I highly recommend this hotel.

<Author>STUNTS4FILM
<Content>Look no place else Let me begin by telling you that I researched hotels in DC for about 6 months before traveling there so it's safe to say I looked into most of the big name hotels. I got a travelers guide from the Visitors Bureau and looked at each and every hotel in their book.The Embassy Suites isn't right for everyone but it fit our needs perfectly and may fit yours as well.We were traveling with our children ages 12 and 15 so we wanted enough room to allow them privacy and have a place for us to unwind after a day of walking so the idea of a suite was a must for us. The Embassy Suites offer a true suite design with a bedroom that is totally seperate from the living room. Some of the suites we looked at were actually just a larger room than a normal hotel room and perhaps had a sitting area so don't be fooled by what some hotels call a suite.Prices will certainly vary depending on the time of year and the occupancy level but we paid $309 per night and was glad to pay it. Other hotels with similar rooms were almost twice this rate.OUTSIDE APPEARANCE: 3 The outside of the ES is nothing to catch your eye but who cares! There are many eye catching hotels in DC but unless you plan on sitting on the curb and admirring the brick work for hours, the outside isn't that important. The drive was clean and the bellmen were dressed nicely and always helpful.LOBBY: 3 Again...who cares. It's nothing to look at. The Concierge is to your left at a small desk and was VERY helpful and friendly. We were greeted within minutes and were checked in less than 5 . The staff were always smiling and friendly...every day.ATRIUM: 5 Near the elevators is the center atrium and it is very nice. There are small waterfalls and beautiful fish that surround the gift shop area with tables and chairs for relaxing at the Managers Special in the evening.ROOM: 5 Our room was nicely decorated, had a flat screen TV, was full of amenitites and the maid service did a WONDERFUL job cleaning it each day. It was big enough to utilize the pull out sofa AND add a roll-away if you wanted to. We had the King Corner suite and I would recommend getting that for the few extra dollars just because it is off-set in the corner and a bit more secluded and perhaps a bit quieter. The King bed was very comfortable, water pressure was good, never ran out of hot water. I did notice something that another reviewer mentioned: the tap water seems a bit warm at all times but aside from brushing my teeth, I never used the tap water. We bought a case of water at CVS and kept it in the refrigerator. The room was very quiet. We were on the 3rd floor but never noticed any traffic noise or the neighbors.FREE BREAKFAST: 5+ How can you go wrong with this. We ate the free breakfast for 4 days in a row. Never had to wait and the food was great! Juice, coffee, omelets, waffles, becon, fresh fruit.... for a family of 4 each meal would have cost about $30-35 and it would have taken more time out of our day. This was a huge factor in our decision to stay at the ES and it was a BIG pay-off.EVENING MGRS SPECIAL:  Can't really rate this because we only did it once. We had some popcorn and a few chips but neither of us drink alcohol so it wasn't a big thing for us. If you do like a cocktail or 2, this is a very neat thing. For 2 hours you are treated to FREE drinks! I noticed several people who seemed to be enjoying this special but for us.... it just wasn't that big of a deal.POOL: 3 Yes...it's true. It's small. If you are looking for a hotel to lay by the pool... look elsewhere. It's indoors, it's small, and it's full of kids. But that didn't stop us from enjoying the hottub. After a day of walking in DC, that hot tub felt pretty good and it's usually a good place to meet some interesting people. LOCATION: 4 There is a CVS pharmacy right around the corner to pick up sodas and snacks and anything you may have forgotten. The guy at the register was stoned out of his mind the first day we were there but at least we got some drinks and snacks.We always used the Foggy Bottom Metro and it's only about 4 blocks away. The walk always felt safe.I looked at many of the other hotels that I researched and considered while I was in DC and I can honestly say that have NO regrets for chosing the Embassy Suites downtown. The manager greeted us daily by name the place was always clean and neat.If you have any questions about traveling to DC...feel free to give me a shout and hopefully I can help.
