<Author>ML006
<Content>Great value for the money We stayed here in June for a long weekend to do some sight-seeing with our family of six (age range of kids - 8 to 20). All in all, an excellent experience for the price paid, especially if traveling with kids. This was a typical Embassy Suites in terms of service (i.e., adequate, not excellent), but for the price, I think it was what I expected. The suite was very clean and nicely decorated, with plenty of room for all of us. The breakfast each morning was very good, with lots of selection. The hotel was very crowded, and the staff did a good job keeping things stocked and clearing tables. We never had to wait for a table. We attended the cocktail hour once, which was nice. We also went to the Italian restaurant once for dinner (Saturday night -- -we had not made reservations anywhere becuase we tried to go to ESPN Zone, but the wait for that was over 2 hours, so we decided to try the hotel restaurant). It was a bit over-priced, but the staff was friendly and everyone enjoyed the food. Not the best meal to be found in DC, but if you find yourself without a reservation, I would definately suggest trying it. As I said above, the hotel was very crowded, but I did not notice any noise once we were in our suite. The location is great -- a short walk to two different Metro lines, which gave us flexibility. Walking distance to Dupont Circle, where we ate a few meals and did some shopping. Really, the only negative that I can think of is that every morning the maid opened the door without knocking (the chain was always on, so she never came all the way in, but it was a disturbing way to be woken every morning!). Over all, a great stay for a great price if you are not expecting anything too fancy.

<Author>family4MI
<Content>Great room and fitness center We are a family of 4 (2 adults, 2 kids) who just stayed here from Saturday through Wednesday. We had a corner king - bedroom, larger living room and dining area. This is a great room with kids and worth the extra cost. Because the dining area is the room you enter by the door, both the bedroom and living room are away from the door and any hallway noise. Though the room needs a full length mirror.We flew in early morning, but went to the hotel to drop off our luggage. They were very nice about storing our luggage and even invited us to have breakfast (not sure if that was because we were gold members, but it was appreciated!)The fitness center is the nicest of any hotel I have been to and I have traveled a lot lately. All new Precor ellipticals, treadmills and a bike each with their own tv monitors and headphones - also weights, mats, fitness balls. The pool is small, but not too many DC hotels have pools. Only complaint was that the bike was missing the headphone jack and both the pool area and fitness center need clocks. In the pool area, people kept asking other people for the time.The breakfast was typical of Embassy Suite hotels (great variety and nicely spread out) plus you actually fill an individual bowl with your desired omelette fillings and then they make it. There seemed to be ample staff working, but they were not very quick at cleaning off tables and often forgot about the ones upstairs. The manager's reception offered a great variety of drinks and there were always 2 friendly ladies making the drinks. They also had fresh popcorn, pretzels, chips, salsa  jalapenos.The hotel is more like four blocks from the Foggy Bottom metro stop and little bit farther from Dupont Circle. We actually took the Metro from Reagan and walked with our suitcases from Foggy Bottom - not a bad walk in nice weather. You see a lot of people walking with suitcases and taking the metro. A 7 day pass is $22 and was well worth it.I would stay at this hotel again just for the fitness center alone - but they need to put a clock in there to keep me on schedule! The lobby internet stations are also very handy.

<Author>JanetV
<Content>Perfect for Kids - Just visited Two families of 4 each travelled Friday night to Tuesday night in April. Very clean and nicely decorated rooms. Window in bedroom opens - which I love for fresh air. Three different mirror/sink areas to brush teeth/apply makeup makes it easy to get ready with 4 people in a room.Excellent hotel experience. All rooms open to courtyard and we liked that because if feels safer than long hallways - the older kids (we had two 9 year olds and two 12 year olds) could roam, go to the gift shop, ride the glass elevator, get snacks, etc. Free breakfast was yummy and saved us $$$ every morning for 8 people. Evening cocktail receiption/snacks reception was very nice too. Only drawback would be that the Metro is 4 blocks away so we hardly ever rode it - too far to walk in not-so-nice weather with exhausted kids- but the taxis run on a zone system so most rides to the major sites (the National Mall area, the Smithsonian, etc.) were only $11 or $14 for four of us each way. But even on our most active day it was only about $25 pp/day but we were saving so much money by having one room at the hotel instead of two and by not buying breakfast or drinks later... and taxis are everywhere in D.C. Staff helpful and nice. Remember to tip the ladies that pour the free drinks - they'll appreciate you!We ate at Nicola's (the private restaurant on-site) with the kids. It was very good and the service was excellent but it was pricey so be prepared. Also, if you like a nice glass of wine and the large no-name bottle at the free bar just isn't doing it for you, you can go into Nicola's and they have some nice wines by the glass. We will definitely look for Embassy Suites hotels on future trips.

<Author>FamilyTravelReports
<Content>Family Friendly But.... We stayed at the Embassy Suites the week after Easter 2007.The place was jammed with other families on Spring Break.There is a free breakfast buffet that comes with the room charge. The food is just average and the staff had a hard time keeping up with demand. There were long lines, empty serving dishes and the clean-up crew could barely keep up with the stacks of dirty dishes littering the tables. (This is not a criticism of the staff--they were obviously working very hard). There is a happy hour from 5:30-7:30p each day with free cocktails for parents and snacks for kids. Many parents seemed to stay out in the atrium enjoying their drinks while their kids swam in the nearby pool. The pool was tiny and crowded and many young kids were unsupervised. The chlorine smell was overwhelming.The staff could not keep up with the demand for towels.In the evening, it seems every family has a different idea of the best time for lights out. On Saturday night, there were two different groups of unsupervised young kids running wildly through the halls after 10pm. Neither the hotel management or the parents seemed very concerned about this behavior. Needless to say, that made it pretty tough for the rest of us to get to sleep!Bottom Line: Think twice about visiting D.C. at Spring Break. The crowds can be overwhelming both at the hotels and at the various sites around town.

The rooms are very spacious and service was excellent. Our toilet broke on day 1 and while we were out for dinner the problem was fixed with no inconvenience to us. Staff is extremely friendly the lobby has many internet kiosks for those who need to quickly check email. Drawback: At check in when the pass was given for parking they failed to mention is wasn't part of the hotel fee, a whopping $25 per night. Also a good 10 minute walk to the Metro..ok in nice weather but with little ones and rain it can be a drag. Nevertheless the hotel while a little dated was still clean and met our expecations. Also while we read the pool was small it is actually fine for 3-10 yr olds We would stay again

<Author>NCTravelercatco
<Content>We had a great experience at the Embassy Suites We visited this hotel during spring break, a particularly busy time. Despite the crowds, the hotel staff was courteous, helpful, and efficient. The room was beautiful and very comfortable. The breakfasts were wonderful, and the manager's welcome reception each night was much appreciated. This is a great location, too. The only warning I have for others is that if you are not accustomed to driving in a large city, or don't want to, then use alternate directions to/from the hotel from the ones they give out. They direct everyone right through downtown DC, a harrowing journey for those who are not prepared for such an adventure. We would definitely stay here again.

<Author>RightHereFuggy
<Content>Great for families I love this hotel. It's beautiful without being snobby. The breakfast buffet and the manager's reception help make it a great value! I really didn't care for was how tiny the pool is. I sat poolside and sipped a cocktail while my daughter and niece swam, and I could not believe how many people just sent their kids down to the pool without accompanying them. After a while it became a screaming madhouse of shrieking kids, and we were happy to leave!I also wish the bathrooms were configured so that someone could use the sink and mirror while someone else was otherwise occupied. There is a sink and mirror outside the bathroom, but having one inside with the toilet and shower ties up the whole room. I would stay here again in a heartbeat, though.
